    6. six

    “I don’t want to talk about this right now, Betty,” Jughead said, his voice sounding strained. He turned and walked away from her, disappearing into the darkness.

    Betty watched him go, feeling a sense of helplessness wash over her. She had never felt this way before. She had always been the one to fix things, to make things right. But now, she felt like she had done something wrong, something that couldn’t be fixed.

    Veronica Lodge stepped forward, her green eyes assessing Betty with a look of curiosity.

    “You know, Betty,” Veronica said, her voice low and hushed. “You and Jughead are a lot alike.”

    Betty looked at Veronica, feeling a sense of confusion. She didn’t understand what Veronica meant.

    “You both have a stubborn streak that makes you want to push forward, no matter what,” Veronica continued. “But sometimes, you need to step back and let things play out. You can’t fix everything, Betty. You don’t always have to be the one in charge.”

    Betty watched as Veronica turned and walked away from her, disappearing into the night. She felt like she had been given a revelation, something that had been hidden from her for a long time. She looked out at the parking lot, at Sweet Pea sitting there, covered in dirt and grime from the race.

    She had won the race, but at what cost?
